  3: "Physical Mutations"
  3: "His jaw appears dislocated, but upon closer inspection, the muscles appear to have stretched to enable a larger bite. The teeth are now elongated and very sharp."
  3: "This adaptation likely facilitates transmission of the parasite, since the new teeth can penetrate deeper into a victim\'s flesh."
  3: "His fingers have also grown longer, and the fingernails have hardened into claws. The reason for this is unclear, though I\'ve received several reports that \'drones\' seem to have much greater grip strength than their emaciated frames would suggest."
  3: "A full examination of his organs shows severe decay. Many were likely nonfunctional long before he was killed."
  3: "It\'s unclear how he stayed motile when his body was rotting away, or how such neglect might benefit the parasite."
  3: "The disease, which many have begun to flippantly refer to as \'zombieism\', is caused by a microscopic parasite found primarily in the blood and saliva of infected individuals."
  3: "Parasite Physiology"
  3: "Immediately after a bite, the parasite enters healthy cells near the infection site, multiplying until the host cell bursts and releases new parasites into the bloodstream. From there, they quickly spread to all major organs, especially the brain."
  3: "Oral concentrations of the parasite are orders of magnitude higher than those found in the blood, which suggests that bites are the only reliable means of transmitting the parasite. This is consistent with our observations."
  3: "Fortunately, the parasite itself is relatively fragile and cannot survive for more than a few minutes outside of the body. Individuals exposed to infected blood are unlikely to become infected themselves unless the blood enters the mouth, eyes, or an open wound."
  3: "But our inability to study live samples in a controlled setting severely limits our ability to test possible cures."
  3: "However, we have found in a small number of cases that a victim <i>can</i> fight off the infection. It\'s unclear why they survive when so many perish, though some medics claim an increased survival rate with the use of certain medications."
  3: "However, this data is complicated by the fact that wounds sustained during an attack are often fatal in their own right, due to the infected\'s aggression and the enhancements to teeth and claws."
